**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

    Second Check After Step 4

    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

**Revisions made:**

1. Consolidated the previous Areas 1 (Executive Actions) and 5 (DOGE) into a single Area 1, since DOGE is part of the executive branch operations.

2. Reorganized topics to create more logical groupings, particularly in the economic area to better reflect tax policy news.

3. Refined the Political Landscape area to better capture the political dynamics evident in the news feed.

4. Created more specific topics in the International Relations area to address the focus on US-China relations and the Russia-Ukraine conflict.

5. Reduced from 8 areas to 7 areas, keeping related categories together while maintaining a structure that can accommodate all news articles.

This revised structure provides clearer organization for congressional briefings and reflects the actual content distribution in the news feed.

**Step 2 (logic-heavy)**

Put Articles into Categories: 

Cluster the hundreds of news articles into the these areas and topics you defined in Step 1. You must put **each** news article **uniquely** into one area and then one topic under area, and you can decide what the best choice is. Grab the news articles by their entire JSON lines for future reference. First, for each article, make your best decision, and write out the categories in front of JSON lines, for future reference. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three. You do not need to sort the JSON lines yet. Those JSON lines should still maintain their original ascending order according to their IDs. Compile all your results in a simple text file (step2.txt).

The step2.txt should contain something like this:

[Area 2: xxx / Topic 2.3: xxx] {"id": 33, "domain": "xxx", "title": "xxx"}

[Area 1: xxx / Topic 1.4: xxx] {"id": 35, "domain": "xxx", "title": "xxx"}

Let me make it clear again: These lines will be still ranked by their IDs in ascending order, just as they were first given in Step 1, **not** their area and topic orders yet. Because sorting according to area and topic is harder, we will do that sorting later.

Let me make it clear again: one news article always belongs to one and **only one** topic, which belongs to one area. In the list, we should never see an article appear twice. We should never be unable to find an article. Please assign one unique areas and one unique topic under that area to each article.

DAILY BRIEFING: APRIL 2025

1. Executive Branch Operations & Restructuring

1.1. Agency Restructuring & Personnel Changes  
Federal agencies face significant staff reductions as FEMA loses approximately 20% of its permanent staff, including longtime leaders, just ahead of hurricane season [1]. This comes as Trump's cabinet appears to be reasserting authority while Elon Musk steps back from his DOGE leadership role [2]. Internal tension is evident, with reports of Musk engaging in a shouting match with Scott Bessent in the West Wing [3]. Other agencies facing turmoil include the Department of Transportation, which initially invited resignations but now scrambles to retain essential personnel [4]. Scientific communities are racing to preserve decades of data from deletion [5], and the FDA is suspending its quality-control program for food testing due to staff cuts [6].

1.2. Executive Orders & White House Controversies  
President Trump has signed multiple executive orders targeting higher education, focusing on accreditation processes and diversity initiatives [1]. These actions explicitly target colleges and schools' equity efforts [2] and aim at "Restoring Equality Opportunity and Meritocracy" [3], including specific efforts to "rein in DEI" programs. The administration has also cut federal grants to a plantation museum focused on slavery [4].

Simultaneously, Trump's cryptocurrency activities have drawn attention, with the President offering a private dinner to the top 220 investors in his memecoin [5] – an offer that caused the previously "fizzled" coin to surge in value [6]. White House VIP tours are reportedly being offered to crypto coin buyers [7].

2. Economic & Trade Policy

2.1. Tariffs & Trade Disputes  
The Trump administration's tariff policies face multiple challenges, including legal action from a dozen Democratic state attorneys general. New York Attorney General Letitia James and 11 others have filed a lawsuit alleging the president's tariffs were "illegally imposed" and constitute a tax hike [1]. China has explicitly contradicted Trump's claims about trade negotiations, stating "there are no negotiations with the US over tariffs" [2]. Businesses express alarm, with one CEO with 500 workers describing the tariff policy as "catastrophic" and filing his own lawsuit [3]. Trump has suggested that 25% auto tariffs "could go up" for Canada "at some point" [4], while critics argue these policies undermine his own reshoring goals [5].

2.2. Financial Markets & Tax Policy  
President Trump's economic agenda faces significant market resistance, with reports indicating Trump has "met his match" in the markets [1], forcing him to reverse course on major economic decisions [2]. On the tax front, Trump and House Speaker Johnson have rejected proposals to increase taxes on wealthy Americans [3], with Trump specifically dismissing the idea of raising taxes on millionaires [4]. At the state level, New York Democrats are pushing to reinstate a state tax on stock sales [5], while California has achieved a milestone in becoming the world's 4th largest economy [6].

3. Immigration & Border Enforcement

3.1. Deportations & Enforcement Actions  
Immigration enforcement has intensified, with international students receiving email notifications that their visas have been revoked and they must "self-deport" [1]. A Minnesota man has spoken out about how his student visa revocation "shattered" his life [2]. The deportation process has been marked by errors, with thousands of people, including U.S. citizens, reportedly receiving surprise deportation notices by email [3]. In one notable case, a Trump-appointed judge has ordered the White House to return a deported migrant [4].

Enforcement actions are affecting long-term residents as well, with a California man who had been in the United States for 35 years detained by ICE while on a school run [5]. Meanwhile, the government has spent over $500,000 on hyper-targeted YouTube advertisements designed to discourage irregular migration [6].

President Trump's public support is declining across multiple metrics. Recent polling shows his approval rating has sunk significantly [1], with a 7-point drop since February [2] and decreases across nearly all key demographic groups [3]. The political landscape reveals complex dynamics within and between parties. Representative Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez is reportedly seeing increased popularity among New York Republicans [6]. The Democratic National Committee has issued an ultimatum to activist David Hogg [7], while Senator Bernie Sanders has stated that Democrats have "paid a political price" for not listening to the working class [8].

The Russia-Ukraine conflict continues to escalate, with Russia launching attacks on Kyiv that have killed at least 8 people [1]. The Trump administration's approach to the conflict is under scrutiny, with analysis suggesting Trump has plans to "sell out Ukraine to Russia" [2]. President Trump has criticized Ukrainian President Zelenskyy for rejecting Ukraine-Russia negotiations, claiming that a deal was "very close" [3].
